[AI]: The concept of "culture" has a rich history and multifaceted meaning, evolving significantly over time. Here's a breakdown of its origin, evolution, and content:

**Origin and Etymology:**

The word "culture" originates from the Latin word *colere*, initially meaning "to cultivate," "to till," or "to take care of," primarily in the context of agriculture [info-library](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQH_Rvd3e4esiWThvB5H20cL_Wylg2QmpR9Fa6vVUbqGPzyAIl3ad2IX9e1erfDxNYNUUyCkQlLwmQIjOCFYPnuUvdPX6_PralVMw-Mdf_ZMcTsq3RRyxUmyV0aVuJyNR1F5fsu7TepEPobrpkm3h_g=) [faktyday](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQF8w-QjmCRGTajEKIWEs6314s3Yiv9ckIyre8fIgFFZnH4PntJgW94vDZ8EwSIhvdMWCg99vwipxZYCr4T_THhaPYEkQ_FktsoTdkIn8JmJr70_NmyE7NxBaSiSka2DH57QPYJPpxSYb7dwAmGWxklj-jC5HVGE2l-NKA==) [wikipedia](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQEi4kYPNPxNNheGCUwP5PDniJgvPI0SDL4KhbUGJFj3LMcOX2IMubVHvTwDPkaosZPER3N-gdOhYYayE1CRnyoNWD-Dx9C1GnXh6zrlA-itq4hJiTvEpkyRUJENvu0UKJ1xGlK0S8bTLYYFeTT3XQm9M2q8F_QkYkkM4bbTmmyHS-mF0gMWH9IM). The first recorded use of the word "cultura" is in Marcus Porcius Cato the Elder's treatise on agriculture, "De agri cultura" [naurok](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQEXFlkVY0CRGzO3Y0dB_f7tWA9RhOxt2Wd-pPowgRcJk3o1t-w0SPFFpWErHQHUHroS800LWcp8gg6_2Q0uDY3ujuGSMuwqgAPEJUsjFi1U1zD1QgDmyD7R4W3Kupc3hRSZWRZ30OpkXjGQM_7bOHGpblKlXlB2xYudxbRYMj5cmTWUZKXaqxonXF6wJkca0n501c0WMJAL7K2IV5MA1f6YvbioMVAoEcFNlNMcS2GTM2W2Mbu78KND7qE=) [studfile](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQE1wzW-BJX9f1QeEhOtflQcekt7iabhYNjZgfB40jJrpXhB1YQPg9zCL-oPiA7v_TXTeeEwfpgRFkjA4W_ums-7iBqHqDTK0btc0yPKmxFt4MTS_gzeqEe8c4WpS8ufhTz7EgLQLOxW) [wikipedia](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQGXNROyRbgSRZQMICRgZdI3_XzsTV1LOrj9IbXWXeM0GOjLJfupu5hqjwW7MOzvrkU_M9XY-3F9eMkW6GNQITT7yUro3K3lSlaBBXEtfyh3Aurseht3a1_cF99gN62MHV1EPNA9KXT__Vrwckq9pyBXHt0qPnAfNKtu0J--vWmPfEmK6IgLq0a-BQ==). Later, Cicero used the term *cultura animi* to refer to the cultivation of the soul or mind through philosophy, highlighting spiritual and intellectual development [info-library](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQH_Rvd3e4esiWThvB5H20cL_Wylg2QmpR9Fa6vVUbqGPzyAIl3ad2IX9e1erfDxNYNUUyCkQlLwmQIjOCFYPnuUvdPX6_PralVMw-Mdf_ZMcTsq3RRyxUmyV0aVuJyNR1F5fsu7TepEPobrpkm3h_g=) [osvita](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQFWYiKZkkf55sFj8oVZ_qyqv8EhxDtXeeobc03VtGpcTYf7apZWs7rE0CYF0NX9Uw_trhBOaTRD9uyYS5upuxgH73htFDK8T6aNJif-OkinYVrNnZI7Ts1TQeK-f5oYn6sszt0JO94k).

**Evolution of the Concept:**

*   **Ancient Times:** In ancient Greece, "paideia" represented culture as the process of forming a cultured person, emphasizing reason, aesthetics, and civic responsibility [History Library].
*   **Middle Ages:** With the rise of Christianity, "culture" was understood as overcoming human limitations through spiritual self-improvement [History Library]. The concept was associated with urban life [osvita](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQFWYiKZkkf55sFj8oVZ_qyqv8EhxDtXeeobc03VtGpcTYf7apZWs7rE0CYF0NX9Uw_trhBOaTRD9uyYS5upuxgH73htFDK8T6aNJif-OkinYVrNnZI7Ts1TQeK-f5oYn6sszt0JO94k).
*   **Renaissance:** Culture was linked to human perfection [osvita](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQFWYiKZkkf55sFj8oVZ_qyqv8EhxDtXeeobc03VtGpcTYf7apZWs7rE0CYF0NX9Uw_trhBOaTRD9uyYS5upuxgH73htFDK8T6aNJif-OkinYVrNnZI7Ts1TQeK-f5oYn6sszt0JO94k) [Studies.In.Ua].
*   **17th Century:** The word "culture" acquired independent scientific significance, signifying the result of human achievements [osvita](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQFWYiKZkkf55sFj8oVZ_qyqv8EhxDtXeeobc03VtGpcTYf7apZWs7rE0CYF0NX9Uw_trhBOaTRD9uyYS5upuxgH73htFDK8T6aNJif-OkinYVrNnZI7Ts1TQeK-f5oYn6sszt0JO94k) [Studies.In.Ua]. German jurist Samuel Pufendorf used it to denote the results of social human activity [wikipedia](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQGXNROyRbgSRZQMICRgZdI3_XzsTV1LOrj9IbXWXeM0GOjLJfupu5hqjwW7MOzvrkU_M9XY-3F9eMkW6GNQITT7yUro3K3lSlaBBXEtfyh3Aurseht3a1_cF99gN62MHV1EPNA9KXT__Vrwckq9pyBXHt0qPnAfNKtu0J--vWmPfEmK6IgLq0a-BQ==) [megalib](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQF2SoT-qkxFEtPe0fgPE2CQGJ3KVWNQRSJvlSpOUyQYhPPjUvmhrkWl3LBXq0YO_TKsVpKZXS9WW2sbbOzKyXuA4vWb3blLrp0w7Qorx8JKsFRSHOvYf5cK2F-1kO9Dq025rnE4Ytil0nAkyEz9KXCbQL2OFFortIqioVBpAql1XjO7A6ObrO_aAy68-WSyHBdmGImz9x84DYsGugPuST_QuitAB8SCXEWVBlGMmcYZ1I2WA9Hz9ubb94UIodjbvw==).
*   **18th-19th Centuries:** Culture began to be viewed as an independent phenomenon in social life [History Library]. Enlightenment thinkers recognized the contradiction between nature and culture [History Library].
*   **Post-Classical Philosophy:** Nietzsche argued that culture was created to suppress people [History Library].
*   **20th and 21st Centuries:** Existentialism emphasizes individual experience and the search for meaning [salleurl](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQEZKbAR6Y6M7lKbVhLu6afkS3R8osu4LkVmu6C_fJ3DBLELYTLCf6neZvRdydX7IPGXxrSuv9hSL-DIsH7hvF2zYorvPk7XlDPCTmjUU4w6qVv7IjKl-uCyen8b2racijgFLicnqDoCQRDTEKcVjnMiJE2OJK8Wf3_Dnyfs0AbUBpt75g==) [fiveable](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQGl2gqlWCNKFC9uGgWQbPS0sYHtdGNXJqLrD-v8_RoMrFA7QaEefhiY6-g_0eVSpKh3ELZsiVKUVezVt37yJau4B2hk52RL_QDd6_RyPK6yLxp3KYHFYdmLmTNdXSMOJH3J4Q7s45RkJ4Fb18R3rBFmLxTgs1DW84UNJMkkuyLgjfxUqKhdrjzGOSXpVMKk0_dSGMYh9v1uUAbWXL4LAFXGfQ--UzFfSjP8Vq1gj9mdvSX7), while postmodernism challenges traditional notions of truth and celebrates diversity [salleurl](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQEZKbAR6Y6M7lKbVhLu6afkS3R8osu4LkVmu6C_fJ3DBLELYTLCf6neZvRdydX7IPGXxrSuv9hSL-DIsH7hvF2zYorvPk7XlDPCTmjUU4w6qVv7IjKl-uCyen8b2racijgFLicnqDoCQRDTEKcVjnMiJE2OJK8Wf3_Dnyfs0AbUBpt75g==) [fiveable](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQGl2gqlWCNKFC9uGgWQbPS0sYHtdGNXJqLrD-v8_RoMrFA7QaEefhiY6-g_0eVSpKh3ELZsiVKUVezVt37yJau4B2hk52RL_QDd6_RyPK6yLxp3KYHFYdmLmTNdXSMOJH3J4Q7s45RkJ4Fb18R3rBFmLxTgs1DW84UNJMkkuyLgjfxUqKhdrjzGOSXpVMKk0_dSGMYh9v1uUAbWXL4LAFXGfQ--UzFfSjP8Vq1gj9mdvSX7). **Structure of Culture:**

*   **Material Culture:** Encompasses the sphere of human production and its results, such as tools, housing, and infrastructure [karapuziki](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQGDb9yH_InkzHsiM2ceN0AxhCGQrYmpQ2WDylbSIcFQjc03wwPRnudIwsirm0kg6H2EaoZJXAuPPNpKfnc8qVKQPfTZZ3pUXRVdzckHWL-jS8ZXGPLor8G-SBIsgh6bFpUwB8MCPLFDnZs9Y_4DeGcdFoaZOW3RfZZekwPk_UIkvFgpkR40Hu8XiBCaPXSeVqw=) [faktyday](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQF8w-QjmCRGTajEKIWEs6314s3Yiv9ckIyre8fIgFFZnH4PntJgW94vDZ8EwSIhvdMWCg99vwipxZYCr4T_THhaPYEkQ_FktsoTdkIn8JmJr70_NmyE7NxBaSiSka2DH57QPYJPpxSYb7dwAmGWxklj-jC5HVGE2l-NKA==) [wikipedia](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQEi4kYPNPxNNheGCUwP5PDniJgvPI0SDL4KhbUGJFj3LMcOX2IMubVHvTwDPkaosZPER3N-gdOhYYayE1CRnyoNWD-Dx9C1GnXh6zrlA-itq4hJiTvEpkyRUJENvu0UKJ1xGlK0S8bTLYYFeTT3XQm9M2q8F_QkYkkM4bbTmmyHS-mF0gMWH9IM).

*   **Походження:** Термін "культура" походить від латинського слова "cultura", яке спочатку означало "обробіток", "догляд за землею" (agricultura). Воно походить від дієслова "colere", що має багато значень, включаючи "обробляти", "вирощувати", "населяти", "шанувати", "поклонятися" та "доглядати".
*   **Перше використання:** Вперше слово "культура" зустрічається в трактаті про землеробс [naurok](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-0) [studfile](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-1) [wikipedia](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-2) [goroh](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-3) [znu](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-4) [esu](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-5) [uahistory](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-6)тво Марка Порція Катона Старшого (234-149 до н.е.) Based on the search results, here's a synthesis of information regarding the evolution of the concept of "culture" in history:

**1. Origin and Etymology:**

*   The word "culture" originates from the Latin word *colere*, meaning "to cultivate," "to till," or "to take care of" (Studies.In.Ua, History Library, Освіта.UA). Initially, it related to agricultural labor (History Library).
*   Cicero later used the term to r [info-library](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-0)efer to the cultivation of the soul or mind (*cultura animi*) through philosophy, emphasizing the spiritual and intellectual development of a person (Osvita.UA, History Library).

**2. Historical Development of the Conce [nkkep](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-1)pt:**

*   **Ancient Times:** "Paideia" in ancient Greece represented culture as the process of forming a cultured person, emphasizing reason, aesthetics, harmony with nature, and civic responsibility (History Library).
*   **Middle Ages:** With the rise of Christianity, "culture" was understood as overcoming human limitations and sinfulness through spiritual self-improvement and recognizing a spiritual connection with God (History Library). The concept was associated with urban life (Osvita.UA).
*   **Renaissance:** Culture was li [osvita](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-2)nked to human perfection (Osvita.UA, Studies.In.Ua).
*   **17th Century:** The word "culture" acquired independent scientific significance (Osvita.UA, Studies.In.Ua). It began to signify the result of h [osvita](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-2)uman achievements that elevate humanity (History Library).
*   **18th-19th Centuries:** Culture began to be viewed as an independent phenomenon in social life, with theoretical reflection on the phenomenon emerging (History Library). The Enlightenment thinkers recognized the contradiction between nature and culture (History Library). Thinkers like Herder saw culture as a historical stage in the improvement of humanity, linked to the development of science and education (History Library).

Nietzsche argued that culture was c [osvita](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-2)reated to suppress and enslave people (History Library).

Culture is often defined as the totality of material and spiritual values created by humankind (Vertexaisearch, Studies.In.Ua), encompassing science, education, art, morality, and worldview (Vertexaisearch).

**3. Key Aspects of Culture:**

*   **Material and Spiritual Culture:** Material culture includes the sphere of human production and its results (tools, housing, etc.), while spiritual culture encompasses consciousness, knowledge, morality, education, science, art, and religion (Vertexaisearch, Studies.In.Ua).
*   **Functions of Culture:** Cultu [buklib](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-4) [osvita](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-2)re has various functions, including cognitive, informative, communicative, regulatory, axiological (value-based), worldview-related, and educational functions (Vertexaisearch).
*   **Culture as a System:** Culture can be seen as a system of values, norms, and artifacts (Vertexaisearch). Values are ideas about what is important in life (Vertexaisearch).

*   Cu [sumdu](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-5) [wikipedia](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-6)ltural [nkkep](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-1) evolution refers to the evolution of human behavior and abilities (Vertexaisearch). *   **Deconstruction:** Questioning fixed meanings in language [12]. [fiveable](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-3) [numberanalytics](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-11)

In summary, both existentialism and postmodernism have significantly shaped the understanding of culture in the 20th and 21st centuries, albeit in different ways. Existentialism emphasizes individual experience and the search for meaning, while postmodernism challenges traditional notions of truth and celebrates diversity and fragmentation. [insidehighered](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-2) The rise of therapeutic culture and self-help movements also played a role in its decline [9]. [numberanalytics](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-6) [journalism](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-7) [numberanalytics](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-8) It rejects grand narratives and universal truths, emphasizing subjectivity, language, and power structures [4, 12, 17, 21]. [numberanalytics](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-10) It has led to a proliferation of diverse and fragmented narratives, challenging traditional storytelling [2]. [numberanalytics](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-10)\n*   **Influence on Identity and Culture:** Postmodernism has challenged modernist notions of a unified and coherent self, highlighting the multiple and fragmented nature of identity and celebrating cultural diversity [3]. [numberanalytics](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-11) [numberanalytics](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-8) [journalism](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-7) It is closely associated with the rise of identity politics, emphasizing the social and political dimensions of identity [4]. [numberanalytics](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-11) Common features include pastiche, irony, hyperreality, and intertextuality [3].\n*   **Impact on Media and Popular Culture:** Postmodernism has had a significant influence on media and popular culture, leading to diverse and fragmented representations [2]. [numberanalytics](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-10) [journalism](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-7) The rise of reality TV, for example, has blurred the lines between reality and simulation [2].\n*   **Cultural Relativism:** Postmodernism is associated with cultural relativism, the idea that no culture has a truer worldview than any other [6].\n*   **Shift in Cultural Studies:** Postmodernism marks a profound shift in how we think about culture, identity, and power in a globalized world [4]. [journalism](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-7) It challenges traditional ways of analyzing culture, advocating for a more fluid, fragmented, and contested approach [4]. [numberanalytics](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-6) It has also been seen as promoting a culture of fragmentation and division [17]. [numberanalytics](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-8)\n\n**Key Concepts of Postmodernism:**\n\n*   **Hyperreality:** The idea that our experiences are shaped by simulations rather than reality itself [3].
